Section 1:
Minority Report
A-Engrossed
Senate Bill 1507
Ordered by the Senate February 13
Including Senate Minority Report Amendments dated February 13
Sponsored by nonconcurring members of the Senate Committee on Finance and Revenue: Senators ANDERSON,
MCLANE
SUMMARY
The following summary is not prepared by the sponsors of the measure and is not a part of the body thereof subject
to consideration by the Legislative Assembly. It is an editor’s brief statement of the essential features of the
measure. The statement includes a measure digest written in compliance with applicable readability standards.
Digest: The Act updates the tie date to the federal Internal Revenue Code and other
federal tax laws. Disconnects from certain federal tax laws. Increases the amount of the
earned income tax credit. (Flesch Readability Score: 60.2).
[Digest: The Act would reduce income taxes and other taxes if the state collects a retail sales tax.
(Flesch Readability Score: 70.1).]
[Reduces taxes imposed under various tax programs, operative conditioned upon imposition of a
statewide retail sales tax dedicated to specified purposes. Directs the Department of Revenue to estimate
the revenue lost to tax reductions and to direct an equal amount of revenue to various purposes.]
Updates the connection date to the federal Internal Revenue Code and other provisions
of federal tax law. Increases the amount of the earned income tax credit allowed as a per-
centage of the federal earned income tax credit.
Applies to tax years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.
Takes effect on the 91st day following adjournment sine die.

23 SECTION 5. ORS 238A.125 is amended to read:
24 238A.125. (1) Upon retiring at normal retirement age, a vested pension program member shall
25 be paid an annual pension for the life of the member as follows:
26 (a) For service as a police officer or firefighter, 1.8 percent of final average salary multiplied
27 by the number of years of retirement credit attributable to service as a police officer or firefighter.
28 (b) For service as other than a police officer or firefighter, 1.5 percent of final average salary
29 multiplied by the number of years of retirement credit attributable to service as other than a police
30 officer or firefighter.
31 (2) Notwithstanding any provision of ORS 238A.100 to 238A.250, the annual benefit payable to
32 a member under the pension program and under any other tax-qualified defined benefit plan main-
33 tained by the participating public employer may not exceed the applicable limitations set forth in
34 26 U.S.C. 415(b), as in effect on December 31, [2023] 2025. The Public Employees Retirement Board
35 shall adopt rules for the administration of this limitation, including adjustments in the annual dollar
36 limitation to reflect cost-of-living adjustments authorized by the Internal Revenue Service.
37 (3) The board shall make no actuarial adjustment in a member’s pension calculated under this
38 section by reason of the member’s retirement after normal retirement age.
39 SECTION 6. ORS 238A.125, as amended by section 3, chapter 101, Oregon Laws 2024, is

41 238A.125. (1) Upon retiring at normal retirement age, a vested pension program member shall
42 be paid an annual pension for the life of the member as follows:
43 (a) For service as a police officer or firefighter, 1.8 percent of final average salary multiplied
44 by the number of years of retirement credit attributable to service as a police officer or firefighter.
45 (b) For service in a hazardous position, 1.8 percent of final average salary multiplied by the
[9]
MR A-Eng. SB 1507
1 number of years of retirement credit attributable to service in a hazardous position.
2 (c) For service as other than a police officer or firefighter or in a hazardous position, 1.5 percent

37 the United States Department of Agriculture, for new housing construction, acquisition of housing
38 or a preservation project; or
39 (B) 20 years, for any other type of qualified loan.
40 (8) The Housing and Community Services Department may certify qualified loans that are eligi-
41 ble under subsection (5) of this section if the total credits attributable to all qualified loans eligible
42 for credits under this section and then outstanding do not exceed $35 million for any fiscal year. In
43 making loan certifications under subsection (7) of this section, the Housing and Community Services
44 Department shall attempt to distribute the tax credits statewide, but shall concentrate the tax
45 credits in those areas of the state that are determined by the Oregon Housing Stability Council to
[27]
MR A-Eng. SB 1507
1 have the greatest need for affordable housing.
2 (9) The tax credit provided for in this section may be taken whether or not:
3 (a) The financial institution is eligible to take a federal income tax credit under section 42 of
4 the Internal Revenue Code with respect to the project financed by the qualified loan;
5 (b) The project receives financing from bonds, the interest on which is exempt from federal
6 taxation under section 103 of the Internal Revenue Code; or
7 (c) The project receives moneys from the Elderly and Disabled Housing Fund under ORS 456.535.
8 (10) For a qualified loan defined in subsection (1)(k)(B) of this section financed through the
9 purchase of bonds, the interest of which is exempt from federal taxation under section 103 of the
10 Internal Revenue Code, the amount of finance charge that would have been charged under sub-
11 section (2)(b) of this section is determined by reference to the finance charge that would have been
12 charged if the federally tax exempt bonds had been issued and the tax credit under this section did
13 not apply.
14 (11) A lending institution may sell a qualified loan for which a certification has been executed
15 to a qualified assignee whether or not the lending institution retains servicing of the qualified loan
16 so long as a designated lending institution maintains records, annually verified by a loan servicer,
17 that establish the amount of tax credit earned by the taxpayer throughout each year of eligibility.
18 (12) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, a lending institution that is a community de-
19 velopment corporation organized under the Oregon Nonprofit Corporation Law may transfer all or
20 part of a tax credit allowed under this section to one or more other lending institutions that are
21 stockholders or members of the community development corporation or that otherwise participate
22 through the community development corporation in the making of one or more qualified loans for
23 which the tax credit under this section is allowed.
24 (13) The lending institution shall file an annual statement with the Housing and Community
25 Services Department, specifying that it has conformed with all requirements imposed by law to
26 qualify for a tax credit under this section.
27 (14) Notwithstanding subsection (1)(j) and (m) of this section, a qualified borrower on a loan to
28 finance the construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation of a manufactured dwelling park
29 under subsection (5)(c) of this section must be:
30 (a) A nonprofit corporation, manufactured dwelling park nonprofit cooperative, state govern-
31 mental entity, local unit of government as defined in ORS 466.706 or housing authority; or
32 (b) A nonprofit corporation or housing authority that has a controlling interest in the real
33 property that is financed by a qualified loan. A controlling interest includes a controlling interest
34 in the general partner of a limited partnership that owns the real property.
35 (15) The Department of Revenue may require that a lending institution that has earned the
36 credit and a lending institution that intends to claim the credit jointly file a notice, as prescribed
37 by the Department of Revenue. The notice must comply with ORS 315.056 (2) or 315.058 (2).
38 (16) The Housing and Community Services Department shall provide information to the Depart-
39 ment of Revenue about all certifications executed under this section, if required by ORS 315.058.
40 (17) The Housing and Community Services Department and the Department of Revenue may
41 adopt rules to carry out the provisions of this section.

7 in a hospital, hospice or residential medical care facility;
8 (b) An illness, disease or condition that in the medical judgment of the treating health care
9 provider poses an imminent danger of death, is terminal in prognosis with a reasonable possibility
10 of death in the near future, or requires constant care;
11 (c) Any period of disability due to pregnancy, or period of absence for prenatal care; or
12 (d) Any period of absence for the donation of a body part, organ or tissue, including preoperative
13 or diagnostic services, surgery, post-operative treatment and recovery.
14 (25) “Third party administrator” means a third party that enters into an agreement with the
15 Director of the Employment Department to implement and administer the paid family and medical
16 leave program established under this chapter.
17 (26) “Tribal government” means:
18 (a) A tribal government as defined in ORS 181A.940; or
19 (b) A federally recognized Indian tribe.
20 (27)(a) “Wages” has the meaning given that term in ORS 657.105.
21 (b) “Wages” does not mean contribution amounts paid to the Paid Family and Medical Leave
22 Insurance Fund by an employer on behalf of an employee under ORS 657B.150 (5).
23 SECTION 33. (1) Except as provided in subsections (2) and (3) of this section, the
24 amendments to statutes by sections 1 to 32 of this 2026 Act apply to transactions or activities
25 occurring on or after January 1, 2026, in tax years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.
26 (2) The effective and applicable dates, and the exceptions, special rules and coordination
27 with the Internal Revenue Code, as amended, relative to those dates, contained in federal law
28 amending the Internal Revenue Code and enacted before January 1, 2026, apply for Oregon
29 personal income and corporate excise and income tax purposes, to the extent they can be
30 made applicable, in the same manner as they are applied under the Internal Revenue Code
31 and related federal law.
32 (3)(a) If a deficiency is assessed against any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before
33 January 1, 2026, and the deficiency or any portion thereof is attributable to any retroactive
34 treatment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842,
35 314.011, 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2
36 and 16 to 29 of this 2026 Act, then any interest or penalty assessed under ORS chapter 305,
37 314, 315, 316, 317, 317A or 318 with respect to the deficiency or portion thereof shall be can-
38 celed.
39 (b) If a refund is due any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, and
40 the refund or any portion thereof is due the taxpayer on account of any retroactive treat-
41 ment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842, 314.011,
42 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2 and 16
43 to 29 of this 2026 Act for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, then notwithstanding
44 ORS 305.270 or 314.415 or any other law, the refund or portion thereof shall be paid without
45 interest.

11 SECTION 34. ORS 315.266 is amended to read:
12 315.266. (1)(a) In addition to any other credit available for purposes of ORS chapter 316, an eli-
13 gible resident individual shall be allowed a credit against the tax otherwise due under ORS chapter
14 316 for the tax year in an amount equal to [nine] 14 percent of the earned income credit allowable
15 to the individual for the same tax year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
16 (b) Notwithstanding paragraph (a) of this subsection, for a taxpayer with a dependent under the
17 age of three at the close of the tax year, the credit allowed under this section shall be in an amount
18 equal to [12] 17 percent of the earned income credit allowable to the individual for the same tax
19 year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
20 (2) A resident individual may claim a credit under this section, using either a Social Security
21 number or an individual taxpayer identification number, if, but for section 32(m) of the Internal
22 Revenue Code, the individual would otherwise be eligible to claim a credit under section 32 of the
23 Internal Revenue Code. The credit allowed as provided in this subsection shall equal the percent-
24 age, as stated in subsection (1) of this section, of the amount that would be allowed on a federal
25 return, based on the amount of the individual’s earned income and the other provisions of section
26 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
27 (3) An eligible nonresident individual shall be allowed the credit computed in the same manner
28 and subject to the same limitations as the credit allowed a resident by subsection (1) or (2) of this
29 section. However, the credit shall be prorated using the proportion provided in ORS 316.117.
30 (4) If a change in the taxable year of a taxpayer occurs as described in ORS 314.085, or if the
31 Department of Revenue terminates the taxpayer’s taxable year under ORS 314.440, the credit al-
32 lowed by this section shall be prorated or computed in a manner consistent with ORS 314.085.
33 (5) If a change in the status of a taxpayer from resident to nonresident or from nonresident to
34 resident occurs, the credit allowed by this section shall be determined in a manner consistent with
35 ORS 316.117.
36 (6) If the amount allowable as a credit under this section, when added to the sum of the amounts
37 allowable as payment of tax under ORS 316.187 or 316.583, other tax prepayment amounts and other
38 refundable credit amounts, exceeds the taxes imposed by ORS chapters 314 and 316 for the tax year
39 after application of any nonrefundable credits allowable for purposes of ORS chapter 316 for the tax
40 year, the amount of the excess shall be refunded to the taxpayer as provided in ORS 316.502.
41 (7) The Department of Revenue may adopt rules for purposes of this section, including but not
42 limited to rules relating to proof of eligibility, the furnishing of information regarding the federal
43 earned income credit claimed by the taxpayer for the tax year and policies and guidelines for the
44 determination of the amount of credit allowed under subsection (2) of this section.
45 (8) Refunds attributable to the earned income credit allowed under this section do not bear in-

83rd OREGON LEGISLATIVE ASSEMBLY--2026 Regular Session
Minority Report
A-Engrossed
Senate Bill 1507
Ordered by the Senate February 13
Including Senate Minority Report Amendments dated February 13
Sponsored by nonconcurring members of the Senate Committee on Finance and Revenue: Senators ANDERSON,
MCLANE
SUMMARY
The following summary is not prepared by the sponsors of the measure and is not a part of the body thereof subject
to consideration by the Legislative Assembly. It is an editor’s brief statement of the essential features of the
measure. The statement includes a measure digest written in compliance with applicable readability standards.
Digest: The Act updates the tie date to the federal Internal Revenue Code and other
federal tax laws. Disconnects from certain federal tax laws. Increases the amount of the
earned income tax credit. (Flesch Readability Score: 60.2).
[Digest: The Act would reduce income taxes and other taxes if the state collects a retail sales tax.
(Flesch Readability Score: 70.1).]
[Reduces taxes imposed under various tax programs, operative conditioned upon imposition of a
statewide retail sales tax dedicated to specified purposes. Directs the Department of Revenue to estimate
the revenue lost to tax reductions and to direct an equal amount of revenue to various purposes.]
Updates the connection date to the federal Internal Revenue Code and other provisions
of federal tax law. Increases the amount of the earned income tax credit allowed as a per-
centage of the federal earned income tax credit.
Applies to tax years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.
Takes effect on the 91st day following adjournment sine die.

10 (3) Insofar as is practicable in the administration of this chapter, the department shall apply and
11 follow the administrative and judicial interpretations of the federal income tax law. When a pro-
12 vision of the federal income tax law is the subject of conflicting opinions by two or more federal
13 courts, the department shall follow the rule observed by the United States Commissioner of Internal
14 Revenue until the conflict is resolved. Nothing contained in this section limits the right or duty of
15 the department to audit the return of any taxpayer or to determine any fact relating to the tax li-
16 ability of any taxpayer.
17 (4) When portions of the Internal Revenue Code incorporated by reference as provided in sub-
18 section (2) of this section refer to rules or regulations prescribed by the Secretary of the Treasury,
19 then such rules or regulations shall be regarded as rules adopted by the department under and in
20 accordance with the provisions of this chapter, whenever they are prescribed or amended.
21 (5)(a) When portions of the Internal Revenue Code incorporated by reference as provided in
22 subsection (2) of this section are later corrected by an Act or a Title within an Act of the United
23 States Congress designated as an Act or Title making technical corrections, then notwithstanding
24 the date that the Act or Title becomes law, those portions of the Internal Revenue Code, as so
25 corrected, shall be the portions of the Internal Revenue Code incorporated by reference as provided
26 in subsection (2) of this section and shall take effect, unless otherwise indicated by the Act or Title
27 (in which case the provisions shall take effect as indicated in the Act or Title), as if originally in-
28 cluded in the provisions of the Act being technically corrected. If, on account of this subsection, any
29 adjustment is required to an Oregon return that would otherwise be prevented by operation of law
30 or rule, the adjustment shall be made, notwithstanding any law or rule to the contrary, in the
31 manner provided under ORS 314.135.
32 (b) As used in this subsection, “Act or Title” includes any subtitle, division or other part of an
33 Act or Title.

13 year may be carried forward and offset against the taxpayer’s tax liability for the next succeeding
14 tax year. Any credit remaining unused in the next succeeding tax year may be carried forward and
15 used in the second succeeding tax year, and likewise, any credit not used in that second succeeding
16 tax year may be carried forward and used in the third succeeding tax year, and any credit not used
17 in that third succeeding tax year may be carried forward and used in the fourth succeeding tax year,
18 and any credit not used in that fourth succeeding tax year may be carried forward and used in the
19 fifth succeeding tax year, but may not be carried forward for any tax year thereafter.
20 (5) To be eligible for the tax credit allowable under this section, a lending institution must make
21 a qualified loan by either purchasing bonds, the proceeds of which are used to finance or refinance
22 a loan that meets the criteria stated in this subsection, or making a loan directly to:
23 (a) An individual or individuals who own a dwelling, participate in an owner-occupied commu-
24 nity rehabilitation program and are certified by the local government or its designated agent as
25 having an income level when the loan is made of 80 percent of the area median income or less;
26 (b) A qualified borrower who:
27 (A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation
28 of housing, including housing in the form of a limited equity cooperative; and
29 (B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
30 ment that the:
31 (i) Housing created by the loan is or will be occupied by households earning 80 percent of the
32 area median income or less; and
33 (ii) Full amount of savings from the reduced interest rate provided by the lending institution is
34 or will be passed on, in the form of reduced housing payments, to the tenants or to the holders of
35 proprietary leases in a limited equity cooperative;
36 (c) Subject to subsection (14) of this section, a qualified borrower who:
37 (A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation
38 of housing consisting of a manufactured dwelling park; and
39 (B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
40 ment that the housing will continue to be operated as a manufactured dwelling park during the pe-
41 riod for which the tax credit is allowed;
42 (d) A qualified borrower who:
43 (A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance acquisition or rehabilitation of housing consisting of a
44 preservation project; and
45 (B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
[26]

MR A-Eng. SB 1507
1 ment that the housing preserved by the loan:
2 (i) Is or will be occupied by households earning 80 percent of the area median income or less;
3 and
4 (ii) Is the subject of a rent assistance contract with the United States Department of Housing
5 and Urban Development or the United States Department of Agriculture that will be maintained by
6 the qualified borrower;
7 (e) A qualified borrower who:
8 (A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation
9 of housing; and
10 (B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
11 ment or the governmental party to the rent assistance contract that the housing preserved by the
12 loan:
13 (i) Is or will be occupied by households earning 80 percent of the area median income or less;
14 and
15 (ii) Is the subject of a rent assistance contract with the federal government or with a state or
16 local government that will be maintained by the qualified borrower and that limits a tenant’s rent
17 to no more than 30 percent of their income;
18 (f) A qualified borrower who:
19 (A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance preservation or rehabilitation of housing; and
20 (B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
21 ment that the housing preserved or rehabilitated by the loan:
22 (i) Is or will be occupied by households earning 80 percent of the area median income or less;
23 and
24 (ii) Is currently characterized by financial or physical distress that threatens its ongoing vi-
25 ability as an affordable housing resource; or
26 (g) A qualified mortgage loan fund.
27 (6) A loan made to refinance a loan that meets the criteria stated in subsection (5) of this sec-
28 tion must be treated the same as a loan that meets the criteria stated in subsection (5) of this sec-
29 tion.
30 (7) For a qualified loan to be eligible for the tax credit allowable under this section, the Housing
31 and Community Services Department must execute a written certification for the qualified loan that:
32 (a) States that the qualified loan is within the limitation imposed by subsection (8) of this sec-
33 tion; and
34 (b) Specifies the period, as determined by the Housing and Community Services Department,
35 during which the tax credit is allowed for the qualified loan, not to exceed:
36 (A) 30 years, for a qualified loan with a contract for rent assistance or financing resources from
37 the United States Department of Agriculture, for new housing construction, acquisition of housing
38 or a preservation project; or
39 (B) 20 years, for any other type of qualified loan.
40 (8) The Housing and Community Services Department may certify qualified loans that are eligi-
41 ble under subsection (5) of this section if the total credits attributable to all qualified loans eligible
42 for credits under this section and then outstanding do not exceed $35 million for any fiscal year. In
43 making loan certifications under subsection (7) of this section, the Housing and Community Services
44 Department shall attempt to distribute the tax credits statewide, but shall concentrate the tax
45 credits in those areas of the state that are determined by the Oregon Housing Stability Council to
[27]

MR A-Eng. SB 1507
1 have the greatest need for affordable housing.
2 (9) The tax credit provided for in this section may be taken whether or not:
3 (a) The financial institution is eligible to take a federal income tax credit under section 42 of
4 the Internal Revenue Code with respect to the project financed by the qualified loan;
5 (b) The project receives financing from bonds, the interest on which is exempt from federal
6 taxation under section 103 of the Internal Revenue Code; or
7 (c) The project receives moneys from the Elderly and Disabled Housing Fund under ORS 456.535.
8 (10) For a qualified loan defined in subsection (1)(k)(B) of this section financed through the
9 purchase of bonds, the interest of which is exempt from federal taxation under section 103 of the
10 Internal Revenue Code, the amount of finance charge that would have been charged under sub-
11 section (2)(b) of this section is determined by reference to the finance charge that would have been
12 charged if the federally tax exempt bonds had been issued and the tax credit under this section did
13 not apply.
14 (11) A lending institution may sell a qualified loan for which a certification has been executed
15 to a qualified assignee whether or not the lending institution retains servicing of the qualified loan
16 so long as a designated lending institution maintains records, annually verified by a loan servicer,
17 that establish the amount of tax credit earned by the taxpayer throughout each year of eligibility.
18 (12) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, a lending institution that is a community de-
19 velopment corporation organized under the Oregon Nonprofit Corporation Law may transfer all or
20 part of a tax credit allowed under this section to one or more other lending institutions that are
21 stockholders or members of the community development corporation or that otherwise participate
22 through the community development corporation in the making of one or more qualified loans for
23 which the tax credit under this section is allowed.
24 (13) The lending institution shall file an annual statement with the Housing and Community
25 Services Department, specifying that it has conformed with all requirements imposed by law to
26 qualify for a tax credit under this section.
27 (14) Notwithstanding subsection (1)(j) and (m) of this section, a qualified borrower on a loan to
28 finance the construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation of a manufactured dwelling park
29 under subsection (5)(c) of this section must be:
30 (a) A nonprofit corporation, manufactured dwelling park nonprofit cooperative, state govern-
31 mental entity, local unit of government as defined in ORS 466.706 or housing authority; or
32 (b) A nonprofit corporation or housing authority that has a controlling interest in the real
33 property that is financed by a qualified loan. A controlling interest includes a controlling interest
34 in the general partner of a limited partnership that owns the real property.
35 (15) The Department of Revenue may require that a lending institution that has earned the
36 credit and a lending institution that intends to claim the credit jointly file a notice, as prescribed
37 by the Department of Revenue. The notice must comply with ORS 315.056 (2) or 315.058 (2).
38 (16) The Housing and Community Services Department shall provide information to the Depart-
39 ment of Revenue about all certifications executed under this section, if required by ORS 315.058.
40 (17) The Housing and Community Services Department and the Department of Revenue may
41 adopt rules to carry out the provisions of this section.

37 (G) A member of the Legislative Assembly.
38 (H) A holder of public office as defined in ORS 260.005.
39 (15)(a) “Employer” means any person that employs one or more employees working anywhere in
40 this state or any agent or employee of such person to whom the duties of the person under this
41 chapter have been delegated.
42 (b) “Employer” includes:
43 (A) A political subdivision of this state or any county, city, district, authority or public corpo-
44 ration, or any instrumentality of a county, city, district, authority or public corporation, organized
45 and existing under law or charter;
[44]

MR A-Eng. SB 1507
1 (B) An individual;
2 (C) Any type of organization, corporation, partnership, limited liability company, association,
3 trust, estate, joint stock company or insurance company;
4 (D) Any successor in interest to an entity described in subparagraph (C) of this paragraph;
5 (E) A trustee, trustee in bankruptcy or receiver; or
6 (F) A trustee or legal representative of a deceased person.
7 (c) “Employer” does not include the federal government or a tribal government.
8 (16) “Employment agency” has the meaning given that term in ORS 658.005.
9 (17) “Family and medical leave insurance benefits” means the wage replacement benefits that
10 are available to a covered individual under ORS 657B.050 or under the terms of an employer plan
11 approved under ORS 657B.210, for family leave, medical leave or safe leave.
12 (18)(a) “Family leave” means leave from work taken by a covered individual:
13 (A) To care for and bond with a child during the first year after the child’s birth or during the
14 first year after the placement of the child through foster care or adoption;
15 (B) To effectuate the legal process required for placement of a foster child or the adoption of
16 a child; or
17 (C) To care for a family member with a serious health condition.
18 (b) “Family leave” does not mean:
19 (A) Leave described in ORS 659A.159 (1)(a) except for leave to care for a child who requires
20 home care due to an illness, injury or condition that is a serious health condition;
21 (B) Leave described in ORS 659A.159 (1)(b); or
22 (C) Leave authorized under ORS 659A.093.
23 (19) “Family member” means:
24 (a) The spouse of a covered individual;
25 (b) A child or the child’s spouse or domestic partner;
26 (c) A parent or the parent’s spouse or domestic partner;
27 (d) A sibling or stepsibling of a covered individual or the sibling’s or stepsibling’s spouse or
28 domestic partner;
29 (e) A grandparent of a covered individual or the grandparent’s spouse or domestic partner;
30 (f) A grandchild of a covered individual or the grandchild’s spouse or domestic partner;
31 (g) The domestic partner of a covered individual; or
32 (h) Any individual related by blood or affinity whose close association with a covered individual
33 is the equivalent of a family relationship.
34 (20) “Medical leave” means leave from work taken by a covered individual that is made neces-
35 sary by the individual’s own serious health condition.
36 (21) “Parent” means:
37 (a) A biological parent, adoptive parent, stepparent or foster parent of a covered individual;
38 (b) A person who was a foster parent of a covered individual when the covered individual was
39 a minor;
40 (c) A person designated as the legal guardian of a covered individual at the time the covered
41 individual was a minor or required a legal guardian;
42 (d) A person with whom a covered individual was or is in a relationship of in loco parentis; or
43 (e) A parent of a covered individual’s spouse or domestic partner who meets a description under
44 paragraphs (a) to (d) of this subsection.
45 (22) “Safe leave” means leave taken for any purpose described in ORS 659A.272.

MR A-Eng. SB 1507
1 (23) “Self-employed individual” means:
2 (a) An individual who has self-employment income as defined in section 1402(b) of the Internal
3 Revenue Code as amended and in effect on December 31, [2023] 2025; or
4 (b) An independent contractor as defined in ORS 670.600.
5 (24) “Serious health condition” means:
6 (a) An illness, injury, impairment or physical or mental condition that requires inpatient care
7 in a hospital, hospice or residential medical care facility;
8 (b) An illness, disease or condition that in the medical judgment of the treating health care
9 provider poses an imminent danger of death, is terminal in prognosis with a reasonable possibility
10 of death in the near future, or requires constant care;
11 (c) Any period of disability due to pregnancy, or period of absence for prenatal care; or
12 (d) Any period of absence for the donation of a body part, organ or tissue, including preoperative
13 or diagnostic services, surgery, post-operative treatment and recovery.
14 (25) “Third party administrator” means a third party that enters into an agreement with the
15 Director of the Employment Department to implement and administer the paid family and medical
16 leave program established under this chapter.
17 (26) “Tribal government” means:
18 (a) A tribal government as defined in ORS 181A.940; or
19 (b) A federally recognized Indian tribe.
20 (27)(a) “Wages” has the meaning given that term in ORS 657.105.
21 (b) “Wages” does not mean contribution amounts paid to the Paid Family and Medical Leave
22 Insurance Fund by an employer on behalf of an employee under ORS 657B.150 (5).
23 SECTION 33. (1) Except as provided in subsections (2) and (3) of this section, the
24 amendments to statutes by sections 1 to 32 of this 2026 Act apply to transactions or activities
25 occurring on or after January 1, 2026, in tax years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.

27 with the Internal Revenue Code, as amended, relative to those dates, contained in federal law
28 amending the Internal Revenue Code and enacted before January 1, 2026, apply for Oregon
29 personal income and corporate excise and income tax purposes, to the extent they can be
30 made applicable, in the same manner as they are applied under the Internal Revenue Code
31 and related federal law.
32 (3)(a) If a deficiency is assessed against any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before
33 January 1, 2026, and the deficiency or any portion thereof is attributable to any retroactive
34 treatment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842,
35 314.011, 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2
36 and 16 to 29 of this 2026 Act, then any interest or penalty assessed under ORS chapter 305,
37 314, 315, 316, 317, 317A or 318 with respect to the deficiency or portion thereof shall be can-
38 celed.
39 (b) If a refund is due any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, and
40 the refund or any portion thereof is due the taxpayer on account of any retroactive treat-
41 ment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842, 314.011,
42 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2 and 16
43 to 29 of this 2026 Act for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, then notwithstanding
44 ORS 305.270 or 314.415 or any other law, the refund or portion thereof shall be paid without
45 interest.

11 SECTION 34. ORS 315.266 is amended to read:
12 315.266. (1)(a) In addition to any other credit available for purposes of ORS chapter 316, an eli-
13 gible resident individual shall be allowed a credit against the tax otherwise due under ORS chapter
14 316 for the tax year in an amount equal to [nine] 14 percent of the earned income credit allowable
15 to the individual for the same tax year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
16 (b) Notwithstanding paragraph (a) of this subsection, for a taxpayer with a dependent under the
17 age of three at the close of the tax year, the credit allowed under this section shall be in an amount
18 equal to [12] 17 percent of the earned income credit allowable to the individual for the same tax
19 year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
20 (2) A resident individual may claim a credit under this section, using either a Social Security
21 number or an individual taxpayer identification number, if, but for section 32(m) of the Internal
22 Revenue Code, the individual would otherwise be eligible to claim a credit under section 32 of the
23 Internal Revenue Code. The credit allowed as provided in this subsection shall equal the percent-
24 age, as stated in subsection (1) of this section, of the amount that would be allowed on a federal
25 return, based on the amount of the individual’s earned income and the other provisions of section
26 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
27 (3) An eligible nonresident individual shall be allowed the credit computed in the same manner
28 and subject to the same limitations as the credit allowed a resident by subsection (1) or (2) of this
29 section. However, the credit shall be prorated using the proportion provided in ORS 316.117.
30 (4) If a change in the taxable year of a taxpayer occurs as described in ORS 314.085, or if the
31 Department of Revenue terminates the taxpayer’s taxable year under ORS 314.440, the credit al-
32 lowed by this section shall be prorated or computed in a manner consistent with ORS 314.085.
33 (5) If a change in the status of a taxpayer from resident to nonresident or from nonresident to
34 resident occurs, the credit allowed by this section shall be determined in a manner consistent with
35 ORS 316.117.
36 (6) If the amount allowable as a credit under this section, when added to the sum of the amounts
37 allowable as payment of tax under ORS 316.187 or 316.583, other tax prepayment amounts and other
38 refundable credit amounts, exceeds the taxes imposed by ORS chapters 314 and 316 for the tax year
39 after application of any nonrefundable credits allowable for purposes of ORS chapter 316 for the tax
40 year, the amount of the excess shall be refunded to the taxpayer as provided in ORS 316.502.
41 (7) The Department of Revenue may adopt rules for purposes of this section, including but not
42 limited to rules relating to proof of eligibility, the furnishing of information regarding the federal
43 earned income credit claimed by the taxpayer for the tax year and policies and guidelines for the
44 determination of the amount of credit allowed under subsection (2) of this section.
45 (8) Refunds attributable to the earned income credit allowed under this section do not bear in-
